<unchecked> <start> ZARATHUSTRA S INTRODUCTORY SPEECH ON BEYOND MAN AND THE LAST managing attained the age of thirty , Zarathustra left his home and the lake of his home and went into the mountains . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There he rejoiced in his spirit and his loneliness and , for ten years , did not grow weary of it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But at last his heart turned , one morning he got up with the dawn , stepped into the presence of the Sun , and thus spake unto him : Thou great star ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What would be thy happiness , were it not for those for whom thou shines . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For ten years thou hast come up here to my cave . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou wouldst have got sick of thy light and thy journey but for me , mine eagle , and my serpent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But we waited for thee every morning and , receiving from thee thine abundance , blessed thee for it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lo ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am weary of my wisdom , like the bee that hath collected too much honey I need hands reaching out for it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I would fain grant and distribute until the wise among men could once more enjoy their folly , and the poor once more their riches . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For that end I must descend to the depth : as thou dost at even , when , sinking behind the sea , thou gives light to the lower regions , thou resplendent star ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I must , like thee , go down , as men say men to whom I would descend . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then bless me , thou impassive eye that canst look without envy even upon over much happiness ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Bless the cup which is about to overflow so that the water golden flowing out of it may carry everywhere the reflection of thy rapture . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lo ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> This cup is about to empty itself again , and Zarathustra will once more become a man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra stepped down the mountains alone and met with nobody . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But when he reached the woods , suddenly there stood in front of him an old man who had left his hermitage to seek roots in the forest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thus the old man spake unto Zarathustra : No stranger to me is the wanderer : many years ago he passed here . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra was his name but he hath changed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then thou carried thine ashes to the mountains : wilt thou to day carry thy fire to the valleys ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Dost thou not fear the incendiary s doom ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Yea , I know Zarathustra again . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Pure is his eye , nor doth any lurk about his mouth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Doth he not skip along like a dancer ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Changed is Zarathustra , a child Zarathustra became , awake is Zarathustra : what art thou going to do among those who sleep ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> As in the sea thou lives in loneliness , and wert borne by the sea . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> art thou now going to walk on the land ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , art thou going to drag thy body thyself ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Why , said the saint , did I go to the forest and desert ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Was it not because I loved men greatly over much ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now I love God : men I love not . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man is a thing far too imperfect for me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Love of men would jul me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra answered : What did I say of love ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am bringing gifts to men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Do not give them anything , said the saint . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Rather take something from them and bear their burden along with them that will serve them best : if it only serve thyself well ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if thou art going to give them aught , give them no more than an alms , and let them beg even for that No , said Zarathustra , I do not give alms . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am not poor enough for that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The saint laughed at Zarathustra and spake thus : Then see to it that they accept thy treasures ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are suspicious of hermits and do not believe that we are coming in order to give . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In their ears our steps sound too lonely through the streets . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And just when during the night in their beds they hear a man going long before sunrise they sometimes ask : whither goethe that thief ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Go not to men , but tarry in the forest ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Rather go to the animals ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Why wilt thou not be like me , a bear among bears , a bird among birds ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And what doth the saint in the forest ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> asked Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The saint answered : I make songs and sing them , and making songs I laugh , cry and hum : I praise God thus . <end>
<unchecked> <start> With singing , crying , laughing , and humming I praise that God who is my God . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But what gift biggest thou to us ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having heard these words Zarathustra bowed to the saint and said : What could I give to you ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But let me off quickly , lest I take aught from you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thus they parted from each other , the old man and the man like two boys laughing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When Zarathustra was alone , however , he spake thus unto his heart : Can it actually be possible ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> This old saint in his forest hath not yet heard aught of God being dead ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Arriving at the next town which lieth nigh the forests , Zarathustra found there many folk gathered in the market for a performance had been promised by a rope dancer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And Zarathustra thus spake unto the folk : teach you beyond man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man is a something that shall be surpassed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What have ye done to surpass him ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> All beings hitherto have created something beyond themselves : and are ye going to be the ebb of this great tide and rather revert to the animal than surpass man ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What with man is the ape ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> A joke or a sore shame . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man shall be the same for beyond man , a joke or a sore shame . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye have made your way from worm to man , and much within you is still worm . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once ye were apes , even now man is ape in a higher degree than any ape . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who is the wisest among you is but a discord and hybrid of plant and ghost . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But do I order you to become ghosts or plants ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Beyond man is the significance of earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Your will shall say : beyond man shall be the significance of earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I conjure you , my brethren , remain faithful to earth and do not believe those who speak unto you of hopes ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Poisoners they are whether they know it or not . <end>
<unchecked> <start> despises of life they are , decaying and themselves poisoned , of whom earth is weary : begone with them ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once the offence against God was the greatest offence , but God died , so that these offenders died also . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now the most terrible of things is to offend earth and rate the intestines of the inscrutable one higher than the significance of earth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once soul looked contemptuously upon body that contempt then being the highest ideal : soul wished the body meagre , hideous , starved . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus soul thought it could escape body and earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Oh ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> that soul was itself meagre , hideous , starved : cruelty was the lust of that soul ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But ye also , my brethren , speak : what teeth your body of your soul ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is your soul not poverty and dirt and a miserable ease ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , a muddy stream is man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One must be a sea to be able to receive a muddy stream without becoming unclean . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , I teach you beyond man : he is that sea , in him your great contempt can sink . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is the greatest thing ye can experience ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> That is the hour of great contempt . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The hour in which not only your happiness , but your reason and virtue as well turn loathsome . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The hour in which ye say : What is my happiness worth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is poverty and dirt and a miserable ease . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But my happiness should itself justify existence ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The hour in which ye say : What is my reason worth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> longer it for knowledge as a lion for its food ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is poverty and dirt and a miserable ease . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The hour in which ye say : What is my virtue worth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It hath not yet lashed me into rage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How tired I am of my good and mine evil ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> All that is poverty and dirt and a miserable ease ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The hour in which ye say : What is my justice worth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I do not see that I am flame and fuel . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the just one is flame and fuel ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The hour in which ye say : What is my pity worth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is pity not the cross to which he is being nailed who lovett men ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But my pity is no crucifixion . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Spake ye ever like that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Cried ye ever like that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> would that I had heard you cry like that ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not your sin , your moderation cried unto heaven , your in sin even cried unto heaven ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Where is the lightning to lick you with its tongue ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Where is that insanity with which ye ought to be inoculated ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I teach you beyond man : he is that lightning , he is that insanity ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra having spoken thus , one of the folk shouted : We have heard enough of the rope dancer let us see him now ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And all the folk laughed at Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The rope dancer , however , who thought he was meant by that word , started with his performance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But Zarathustra looked at the folk and wondered . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then he spake thus : Man is a rope connecting animal and , a rope over a precipice . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Dangerous over , dangerous on the way , dangerous looking backward , dangerous shivering and making a stand . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is great in man is that he is a bridge and not a goal : what can be loved in man is that he is a transition and a destruction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love those who do not know how to live unless in perishing , for they are those going beyond . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love the great despises because they are the great adores , they are arrows of longing for the other shore . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love those who do not seek behind the stars for a reason to perish and be sacrificed , but who sacrifice themselves to earth in order that earth may someday become beyond man s . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who giveth to perceive , and who is longing for perception in order that some day may live . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thus he willett his own destruction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who workers and invented to build a house for beyond man and make ready for him earth , animal , and plant for thus he willett his own destruction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who lovett his virtue : for virtue is will to destruction and an arrow of longing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who kenneth no drop of spirit for himself , but willett to be entirely the spirit , of his virtue : thus as a spirit crossed he the bridge . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who maketh his virtue his inclination and his fate : thus for the sake of his virtue he willett to live longer and live no more . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who yearned not after too many virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One virtue is more than two because it is so much the more a knot on which to hang fate . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him whose soul waste itself , who neither fl wanted thanks nor returned aught : for he always giveth and seemeth nothing to keep of himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who is ashamed when the dice are thrown in his favour and who then asked : am I a cheat in playing ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> for he desire to perish . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who strewth golden words before his deeds and performed still more than his promise : for he seemeth his own destruction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who justified the future ones and safety the past ones : for he seemeth to perish on account of the present ones . <end>
<unchecked> <start> his God : for he must perish on account of the wrath of his God . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him whose soul is deep even when wounded and who can perish even on account of a small affair : for he gladly crossed the bridge . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him whose soul is over full so that he himself and all things are within him : thus all things become his destruction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who is of a free spirit and of a free heart : thus his head is merely the intestine of his heart , but his heart drive him to destruction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love all those who are like heavy drops falling one by one from the dark cloud lowering over men : they announce the coming of the lightning and perish in the announcing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , I am an announcer of the lightning and a heavy drop from the clouds : that lightning s name is beyond man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having spoken these words Zarathustra again looked at the folk and was silent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There they are standing , he said unto his heart , there they are laughing : they do not understand me , I am not the mouth for these ears . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Must they needs have their ears beaten to pieces before they will learn to hear with their eyes ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Must one rattle like a kettledrums and a fast day preacher ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or do they only believe stammered ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> ZARATHUSTRA S INTRODUCTORY speech I I They have got something to be proud of . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How name they what maketh them proud ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Education they name it it distinguishes them from the goat herds . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wherefore they like not to hear the word contempt used of themselves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I am going to speak unto their pride . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I am going to speak unto them of the most contemptible : that is of the last man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is time for man to mark out his goal . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is time for man to plant the germ of his highest hope . <end>
<unchecked> <start> His soil is still rich enough for that purpose . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But one day that soil will be impoverished and tame , no high tree being any longer able to grow from it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> the time cometh when man will no longer throw the arrow of his longing beyond man and the string of his bow will have lost the cunning to whizz ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I tell you : one must have chaos , within to enable one to give birth to a dancing star . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I tell you : ye have still got chaos within . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> the time cometh when man will no longer give birth to any star ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> There cometh the time of the most contemptible man who can no longer despise himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is love ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is creation ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is longing ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is star ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus the last man asked , blinking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then earth will have become small , and on it the last man will be hopping who maketh everything small . <end>
<unchecked> <start> His kind is indestructible like the ground flea the last man giveth longest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We have invented happiness , the last men say , blinking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They have left the regions where it was hard to live , for one must have warmth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One still lovett his neighbour and rubbish one s self on him for warmth one must have . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To turn sick and to have suspicion are regarded as sinful . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They walk wearily . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A fool he who still stumbled over stones or men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A little poison now and then : that cause pleasant dreams . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And much poison at last for an easy death . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They still work , for work is an entertainment . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But they are careful , lest the entertainment exhaust them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They no longer grow poor and rich it is too troublesome to do either . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No herdsman and one flock ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Each willett the same , each is equal : he who feelers otherwise voluntarily goethe into a lunatic asylum . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once all the world was lunatic the most refined say , blinking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One is clever and knower whatever has happened , so that there is no end of mocking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They still quarrel , but they are soon reconciled otherwise the stomach would turn . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One hath one s little lust for the day and one s little lust for the night : but one honoured health . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We have invented happiness , the last men say , blinking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And here ended Zarathustra s first speech which is also called the introductory speech : for in that moment the shouting and merriment of the folk interrupted him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Give us that last man , o Zarathustra thus they bawled make us that last man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> We gladly renounce beyond man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And all the folk cheered smacking with the tongue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But Zarathustra sadly said unto his heart : They understand me not : I am not the mouth for these ears . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I suppose I lived too long in the mountains , listen ing too much to brooks and trees : now for them my speech is like that of goat herds . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Unmoved is my soul and bright like the mountains in the morning . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But they deem me cold and a mockery with terrible jokes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And now they look at me and laugh : and while they laugh they hate me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is ice in their laughter . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then a thing happened which silenced every mouth and fixed every eye . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For in the meantime the had begun his performance : he had stepped out of the little door and walked along the rope that was stretched between two towers so that it hung over the market and the folk . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When he was just midway the little door opened again and a gay coloured fellow like a clown jumped out and walked with quick steps after the first . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Go on , lame leg , his terrible voice shouted , go on , slow step , smuggler , pale face ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> That I may not tickle thee with my heel ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What dost thou here between towers ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thy place is in the tower . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou shoulds be imprisoned . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou arrest the free course to one who is better than thou art ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And with each word the clown drew nearer and nearer : but when he was just one step behind , the terrible thing happened which silenced every mouth and fixed every eye : uttering a cry like a devil , he jumped over him who was in his way . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The latter seeing his rival conquer , lost his head and the rope throwing down his stick he shot down quicker than it , like a whirl of arms and legs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The market and the folk were as the sea when the storm rushed over it : everybody fled tumbling one over the other , and most there where the body was to strike the ground . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra remained standing there , and the body fell down just beside him , badly disfigured and broken , but not dead . <end>
<unchecked> <start> After a while , the consciousness of the fallen one coming back , he saw Zarathustra kneel beside him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What art thou doing there ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> he asked at last , I knew it long ago that the devil would play me a trick . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now he dragged me unto hell : art thou going to hinder him ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> On my honour , friend , Zarathustra answered , what thou speaker of doth not exist : there is no devil nor hell . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thy soul will be dead even sooner than thy body : henceforward fear nothing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The man looked up suspiciously : If thou speaker truth , he said , losing my life I lose nothing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then I am not much more than an animal which by means of blows and tit bits hath been taught to dance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not so , Zarathustra said thou hast made danger thy calling , there is nothing contemptible in that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now thou diet of thy calling : therefore shall I bury thee with mine own hands . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra having said thus the dying one made no answer , but moved his hand as though he sought Zarathustra s to thank him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Meanwhile the evening fell , and the market was hidden in darkness : the folk dispersed , for even curiosity and terror grow tired . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra , however , sat beside the dead man on the ground , absorbed in thought , forgetting the time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But at last it was night , and a cold wind blew over the lonely one . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then Zarathustra rising said unto his heart : Verily , a fine fishing was Zarathustra s to day ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was not a man he caught , but a corpse . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Haunted is human life and yet meaningless : a buffoon may be fatal to it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am going to teach men their life s significance : which is beyond man , the lightning from the dark cloud of man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But still I am remote from them , my sense speaker not to their sense . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For men I am still a cross between a fool and a corpse . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Dark is the night , dark are Zarathustra s ways . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Come on , thou cold and stiff companion ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I carry thee to the place where I shall bury thee with my hands . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having said thus unto his heart Zarathustra took the corpse on his back and started on his way . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When he had not yet gone a hundred steps , somebody stealing close to him whispered into his ear and lo ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> the speaker was the buffoon from the tower . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Depart from this town , O Zarathustra , he said too many hate thee here . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There hate thee the good and just ones , and they call thee their enemy and despised there hate thee the faithful of the right belief , and they call thee a danger for the many . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was thy good fortune to be laughed at : and , verily , thou spaces like a buffoon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was thy good fortune to associate with the dead dog by thus humiliating thyself thou hast saved thyself to day . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But depart from this town or to morrow I jump over thee , a living over a dead one . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having so said , the man disappeared , whilst Zarathustra went on through the dark lanes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At the gate of the town he met the grave diggers . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They flared their torch in his face , and recognising Zarathustra , mocked him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra is carrying off the dead dog : well that Zarathustra hath turned grave digger ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> For our hands are too clean for this roast . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Perhaps Zarathustra means to steal from the devil his bite ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Go on ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And much luck to the dinner ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> We are afraid the devil will be a better thief than Zarathustra ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> he stealth both of them , he earth both ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And putting their heads together they laughed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra saying no word in answer went his way . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Journeying two hours through forests and swamps , he heard the hungry howling of the wolves and felt hungry himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> So he stopped at a lonely house in which a light was burning . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Hunger surprised me , said Zarathustra , like a robber . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Amid forests and swamps in the depth of the night my hunger surprised me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My hunger hath odd fancies . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Frequently it appeared only after dinner , and to day it did not appear all day : where was it ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And then Zarathustra knocked at the door of the house . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Very soon an old man came carrying a candle and asking : Who cometh to me and mine evil sleep ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> A living and a dead one replied Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Give me to eat and to drink , I forgot it in the daytime . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who feeder the hungry refreshed his own soul thus saith wisdom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The old man having gone off returned immediately , offering Zarathustra bread and wine . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This is a bad quarter for hungry people , said he that is why I am staying here . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Animal and man come to me , the hermit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But ask also thy companion to eat and drink he is much more tired than thou art . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra answered : Dead is my companion I shall scarcely persuade him to do so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That is no reason with me , said the old man crossly he who knocked at my house must take whatever I offer him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Eat and farewell ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then Zarathustra walked two more hours and trusted the road and the light of the stars for he was accustomed to walk by night and liked to look into the face of all things asleep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But when the morning dawned , Zarathustra found himself in a deep forest with no road visible . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then he laid the dead one in a hollow tree at his own head for he wished to defend him from the wolves and he laid himself down on the ground and moss . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And at once he fell asleep , with his body tired , but with his soul unmoved . <end>
<unchecked> <start> ZARATHUSTRA S INTRODUCTORY SPEECH long slept Zarathustra , not only the dawn his face , but the morning also . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At last , however , his eye opened : astonished Zarathustra looked into the forest and the stillness , astonished he looked into himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then quickly rising , like a mariner who suddenly teeth land , he exulted : for he saw a new truth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thus he then spake unto his heart : A light hath arisen for me : companions I need , and living ones , not dead companions or corpses which I carry with me wherever I go . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But living companions I need who follow me because they wish to follow themselves and to the place whither I wish to go . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A light hath arisen for me : Zarathustra is not to speak unto the folk , but unto companions ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra is not to be the herdsman and dog of a herd ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> To entice many from the herd that is why I have come . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Folk and herd will be angry with me : a robber Zarathustra wished to be called by herdsmen . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Herdsmen I call them , but they call themselves the good and just . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Herdsmen I call them , but they call themselves the faithful of the right belief . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lo , the good and just ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whom do they hate most ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Him who breath to pieces their tables of values , the breaker , the criminal : but he is the creator . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lo , the faithful of all beliefs ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whom do they hate most ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Him who breath to pieces their tables of values , the breaker , the criminal : but he is the creator . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Companions the creator seemeth and not corpses , neither herds nor faithful men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Such as will be creators with him the creator seemeth , those who write new values on new tables . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Companions the creator seemeth , and such as will reap with him : for with him everything is ripe for harvest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But he jacket the hundred sickles so that he heareth up the ears and is angry . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Companions the creator seemeth , and such as know how to whet their sickles . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Destroyers they will be called and despises of good and evil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But they are those who reap and cease from labour . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Such as will be creators with him Zarathustra seemeth , such as reap with him and cease from labour with him : what hath he to do with herds and herdsmen and corpses ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thou , my first companion , farewell ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Well I buried thee in thy hollow tree , well I hid thee from the wolves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I part from thee , the time is past . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Between dawn and dawn a new truth hath revealed itself to me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am not to be a herdsman nor yet a grave digger . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am not even to speak unto the folk again . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I have spoken unto a dead one for the last time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Those who are creators , who reap , who cease from labour I shall associate with . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I shall show them the rainbow and all the degrees of beyond man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I shall sing my song unto the hermits and those who are hermits in pairs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And the heart of him who hath ears for unheard things I shall make heavy with my happiness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Towards my goal I struggle , mine own way I go I shall overlap those who hesitate and delay . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let my way be their destruction ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having said thus unto his heart , when the sun was at noon Zarathustra suddenly looked upwards wondering for above himself he heard the sharp cry of a bird . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And lo ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> an eagle swept through the air in wide circles , a serpent hanging from it not like a prey , but like a friend : coiling round its neck . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are mine animals said Zarathustra and rejoiced heartily . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The proudest animal under the sun , and the wisest animal under the sun have set out to reconnoitre . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They wished to learn whether Zarathustra still giveth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , do I still live ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> More dangerous than among animals I found it among men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Dangerous ways are taken by Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let mine animals lead me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having so said Zarathustra thought of the words of the saint in the forest and sighing he thus spake unto his heart : Would I were wiser ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would I were wise from the root like my serpent ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I ask impossibilities . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I ask my pride to be always the companion of my wisdom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when once my wisdom leave me : alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> it lieth to fly away ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would that my pride would then fly with my folly ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Three metamorphoses of the spirit I declare unto you : how the spirit become a camel , the camel a lion , and the lion at last a child . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There are many things heavy for the spirit , the strong spirit which is able to bear the load and in which reverence dwellers : its strength longer for the heavy and heaviest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is heavy ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> asked the spirit which is able to bear the load , and kneeling down like a camel wished to be well laden . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is the heaviest , ye heroes ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> asked the spirit which is able to bear the load , that I may take it on me and rejoice in my strength . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is it not : to humiliate one s self in order to give pain to one s haughtiness ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> To show forth one s folly in order to mock at one s wisdom ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or is it : to part from our cause when it is celebrating its victory ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> To ascend high mountains in order to tempt the tempter ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or is it : to live on the acorns and grass of knowledge and to starve one s soul for the sake of truth ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or is it : to be ill and send away the consoles and make friends of deaf people who never hear thy wishes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or is it : to step into dirty water , if it be the water of truth , and not drive away the cold frogs and hot toads ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or is it : to love those who despise us and to shake hands with the ghost when it is going to terrify us ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> All these heaviest things are taken upon itself by the spirit that is able to bear the load like the camel which when it is laden haste to the desert , the spirit haste to its own desert . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the loneliest desert however cometh the second metamorphosis : there the spirit become a lion . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Freedom it will take as its prey and be lord in its own desert . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There it seemeth its last lord : to him and its last God it seemeth to be a foe , with the great dragon it seemeth to contend for victory . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is the great dragon which the spirit is no longer willing to call lord and God ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou shalt is the name of the great dragon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the lion s spirit saith : I will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou shalt besets his way glittering with gold , a pangolin , on each scale there shine golden Thou shalt . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Values a thousand years old are shining on these scales , and thus saith the most powerful of all dragons : The value of all things is shining on me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All value hath been created , and all value created that is I . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , there shall be no more I will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus saith the dragon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brethren , wherefore is the lion in the spirit necessary ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wherefore doth the beast of burden that renounce and is reverent not suffice ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> To create new values that even the lion is not able to do : but to create for itself freedom for new creating , for that the lion s power is enough . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To create for one s self freedom and a holy Nay even towards duty : therefore , my brethren , the lion is required . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To take for one s self the right to new values that is the most terrible taking for a spirit able to bear the load and reverent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Indeed , for it a preying it is and the work of a beast of prey . <end>
<unchecked> <start> As its holiest it once loved Thou shalt : now it must find illusion and arbitrariness even in the holiest , in order to prey for itself freedom from its love : the lion is required for that preying . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But tell me , my brethren , what can the child do which not even the lion could ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Why must the preying lion become a child also ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The child is innocence and oblivion , a new starting , a play , a wheel rolling by itself , a prime motor , a holy asserting . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ay , for the play of creating , my brethren , a holy asserting is wanted : it is its own will that the spirit now willett , it is its own world that the recluse jinneth for himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Three metamorphoses of the spirit I declare unto you : how the spirit become a camel , the camel a lion , and the lion at last a child . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus spake Zarathustra when he stayed in the town which is called : The Cow of Many Colours . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF THE CHAIRS OF VIRTUE Some one praised a wise man to Zarathustra because he was said to speak well of sleep and virtue and therefore to be very much honoured and rewarded . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All young men were said to sit before his chair . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra went to him and sat among all the young men before his chair . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thus spake the wise man : Honour and shame to sleep ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> That is the first thing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And to go out of the way of all who sleep badly and are awake in the night ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even the thief is ashamed to disturb sleep : he always stealth gently through the night . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But shameless is the watchman of the night , shamelessly he heareth his horn . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Sleeping is no small art : for that purpose one needed firstly to keep awake all day . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ten times a day thou must conquer thyself : that giveth a wholesome weariness and is poppy for the soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ten times thou must reconcile thyself with thyself : for resignation is bitterness and badly sleeper he who is not reconciled . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ten truths a day thou must find : else thou seeks for truth even in the night , thy soul having remained hungry . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ten times a day thou must laugh and be gay : else thy stomach disturbed thee in the night , that father of affliction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Few know that , but in order to sleep well one must have all virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Shall I bear false witness ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Shall I commit adultery ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Shall I covet my neighbour s maid servant ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> All that would ill accord with good sleep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And even if one hath all the virtues , one must know one more thing , to send unto sleep the virtues at the proper time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In order that they may not quarrel , the pretty little women ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And about thee , thou unhappy one ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Peace with God and thy neighbour : good sleep will have it so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And peace even with the neighbour s devil ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Else it will haunt thee in the night Honour and obedience to the magistrates , and even to crooked magistrates ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> good sleep will have it so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is it my fault that power lieth to walk on crooked legs ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> He shall be called by me the best herdsman who leader his sheep unto the greenest meadow : that accorded well with good sleep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I do not want many honours nor great treasures : that the milk . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But one sleeper badly without a good name and a small treasure . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A small society is more welcome unto me than an evil one : it must however come and go at the proper time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That accorded well with good sleep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am also well pleased with the poor in spirit : they promote sleep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Blessed are they , especially if one always yielded to them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus the day passed for the virtuous . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When night cometh I take good care not to call sleep ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It lieth not to be called : sleep which is the master of virtues ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I think of what I did and thought during the day . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ruminating I ask myselF , patient as a cow : what were thy ten resignations ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And what were thy ten reconciliations , and the ten truths and the ten laughter with which my heart pleased itself ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whilst I am meditating thus and rocked by forty thoughts , suddenly sleep seized me : the uncalled one , the master of virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Sleep knocking at mine eye , it gentech heavy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Sleep touching my mouth , it remained open . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , on soft soles it approaches me , the dearest of thieves , stealing my thoughts : stupid I stand like this chair . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having heard the wise man speak thus , Zarathustra laughed in his heart : for a light had arisen for him in the meantime . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thus he spake unto his heart : A fool I consider that wise man there with his forty thoughts but I believe that he well knower how to sleep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Happy he who giveth near this wise man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Such a sleep is infectious , even through a thick wall it is infectious . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A charm giveth even in his chair . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nor did the youths sit in vain before the preacher of virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> His wisdom is : to wake in order to sleep well . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And verily , if life had no significance , and had I to choose nonsense , this nonsense would seem to be the worthies to be chosen for me as well . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now I understand clearly , what once was sought for above all when teachers of virtue were sought . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Good sleep was sought for and poppy head like virtues with it ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> For all those bearded wise men of chairs , wisdom was sleep without dreams : they knowing no better significance of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even to day there are a few extant who are like this preacher of virtues and not always so honest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But their time is past . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And not much longer they stand : there they lie already . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus spake Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF BACK WORLDS MEN Once Zarathustra threw his spell beyond man , like all back worlds men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then the world seemed to me the work of a suffering and tortured God . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A dream then the world appeared to me , and a God s fiction coloured smoke before the eyes of a godlike discontented one . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Good and evil , and pleasure and pain , and I and thou coloured smoke it appeared to me before creative eyes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When the creator wished to look away from himself he created the world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For the sufferer it is an intoxicating joy to look away from his suffering and lose himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> An intoxicating joy and a losing of one s self the world once appeared to me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This world , the ever imperfect , an image and an imperfect image of an eternal contradiction an intoxicating joy to its imperfect creator : thus this world once appeared to me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I threw my spell beyond man , like all backwards men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Truly beyond man ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> brethren , that God whom I created was man s work and man s madness , like all Gods ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man he was , and but a poor piece of man and the I . <end>
<unchecked> <start> From mine own ashes and flame it came unto me , that ghost , yea verily ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It did not come unto me from beyond ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What happened , brethren ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I overcame myself , the sufferer , and carrying mine own ashes unto the mountains invented for myself a brighter flame . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And lo ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> the ghost departed from me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now to me , the convalescent , it would be suffering and pain to believe in such ghosts : suffering it were now for me and humiliation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I speak unto the back worlds men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Sorrow and weakness created all back worlds and that short madness of happiness which only the most sorrowful experience . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Weariness which , with one jump , with a jump of death , wanted to reach the last , a poor ignorant weariness which is not even willing any more to will : it created all Gods and back worlds . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Believe me , my brethren ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was the body which despaired of the body with the fingers of a fooled spirit it groped at the last walls . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Believe me , my brethren ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was the body which despaired of earth , it heard the womb of existence speak unto it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And there it yearned to get through the last walls with its head , and not with its head only beyond , to the other world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the other world is carefully hidden from man , that brutish , inhuman world which is a heavenly nothing and the womb of existence speaker not unto man unless as man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , difficult to be proved is all existence and difficult to be induced to speak . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Tell me , brethren , hath not the oddest of all things been proved even best of all ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ay , that I and the contradiction and confusion of the I speak most honestly of all existence , that creating , willing , valuing I which is the measure and the value of things . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And that most honest existence , that I which speaker of the body and still willett the body even when composing poetry and imagining and fluttering with broken wings . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even more honestly it learned to speak , that I : and the more it learned , the more words and honours for body and earth it finder . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A new pride I have been taught by mine I and this I teach men : no more to put their head into the sand of heavenly things , but to carry it freely , an earth head that giveth significance unto earth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> A new will I teach men : to will that way which man hath gone blindly and to call it good and no longer to shirk aside from it like the sickly and dying . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The sickly and dying folk despised body and earth and invented the heavenly and the redeeming : but even those sweet and gloomy poisons were borrowed from body and earth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> They sought to escape from their misery , and the stars were too remote for them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then they sighed : Would that there were heavenly ways by which to steal into another existence and happiness ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> they invented for themselves their byways and little bloody drinks ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And they professed to be beyond the reach of their body and this earth , the ungrateful ones . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But to whom did they owe the convulsion and delight of their removal ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> To their body and this earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Kind unto the sick is Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , he is not angry at their ways of consolation and ingratitude . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would they were convalescent and conquering and creating a higher body for themselves ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Neither is Zarathustra angry with the convalescent one , if he looked fondly back upon his illusion and at midnight stealth round the grave of his God : but even his tears remain for me a disease and a sick body . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many sick folk were always among the makers of poetry and the god passionate furiously they hate him who perceived and that youngest of virtues that is called honesty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Backward they ever gaze into the dark times : then , of course , illusion and belief were something else . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Intoxication of reason was likeness unto God , and doubt was sin . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Only too well I know those god like ones : they wish to be believed in , and that doubt should be sin . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Only too well I know , besides , what they themselves believe in most . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , not in back worlds and redeeming : but even they believe most in body , and their own body for them is the thing in itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But a sickly thing it is for them : and fain they would leap out of their skin . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore they listen unto the preachers of death and themselves preach back worlds . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Rather listen , my brethren , unto the voice of the body that hath been restored unto health : it is a more honest and a purer voice . <end>
<unchecked> <start> More honestly and purely the healthy body speaker , the perfect and rectangular : it speaker of the significance of earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is unto the despises of body that I shall say my word . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is not to re learn and re teach what I wish them to do I wish them to say farewell unto their own body and be dumb . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Body I am and soul thus the child speaker . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And why should one not speak like the children ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But he who is awake and knower saith : Body I am throughout , and nothing besides and soul is merely a word for a something in body . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Body is one great reason , a plurality with one sense , a war and a peace , a flock and a herdsman . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Also thy little reason , my brother , which thou tallest spirit it is a tool of thy body , a little tool and toy of thy great reason . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I thou safest and art proud of that word . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the greater thing is which thou wilt not believe thy body and its great reason . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It doth not say I , but it doth I . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What the sense feelers , what the spirit perceived hath never its end in itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But sense and spirit would fain persuade thee , that they were the end of all things : so vain they are . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Tools and toys are sense and spirit : behind them there lieth the self . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The self also seemeth with the eyes of the senses , it also listened with the ears of the spirit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The self ever listened and seemeth : it compared , subdued , conquered , destroyed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It rules and is the ruler of the I as well . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behind thy thoughts and feelings , my brother , standish a mighty lord , an unknown wise man whose name is self . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In thy body he dwellers , thy body he is . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is more reason in thy body than in thy best wisdom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And who can know why thy body needed thy best wisdom ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thy self laughed at thine I and its prancing : What are these bounding and flights of thought ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> it saith unto itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A round about way to my purpose . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am the leading string of the I and the suggested of its concepts . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The self saith unto the I : Feel pain here ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And there it suffered and meditate how to get rid of suffering and that is why it shall think . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The self saith unto the I : Feel lust here ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> There it rejoice and meditate how to rejoice often and that is why it shall meditate . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am going to say a word unto the despises of body . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Their contempt maketh their valuing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is it that created valuing and despising and worth and will ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The creative self created for itself valuing and despising , it created for itself lust and woe . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The creative body created for itself the spirit to be the hand of its will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even in your folly and contempt , ye despises of body , ye are serving your self . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I say unto you : your self itself is going to die and turned away from life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No longer is it able to do what it lieth best : to create something beyond itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That it lieth best , that is its whole enthusiasm . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But now it is too late for it to attain that purpose : your self seemeth to perish , ye despises of body . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Your self seemeth to perish and therefore ye are become despises of body ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> For no longer are ye able to create anything beyond yourselves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And therefore are ye now angry at life and earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> An unconscious envy is in the sidelong look of your contempt . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I go not your way , ye despises of body ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye are no bridges to beyond man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brother , when thou hast a virtue and it is thy virtue , thou hast it in common with nobody . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is true thou wilt call it by a name and pet it thou wilt pull its ear and amuse thyself with it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And lo ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> now thou hast its name in common with the folk and hast become folk and herd with thy virtue ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It would be better for thee to say : Unutterable and nameless is that which maketh my soul s pain and sweetness , and it is a hunger of mine intestines . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let thy virtue be too high for the familiarity of names : and if thou hast to speak of it , be not ashamed to stammer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Speak and stammer : That is my good , that love I , thus it pleaseth me entirely , thus alone will I the good . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I do not will it as the law of a God , I do not will it as the statute or requirement of man : it shall not be a landmark for me to beyond earths or paradises . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is an earthly virtue that I love : there is little prudence in it , and still less the reason common to all . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But that bird hath built its nest with me : that is why I love and embrace it , now with me it sitter on golden eggs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once having passions thou called them evil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now , however , thou hast nothing but thy virtues : they grow out of thy passions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou latest thy highest goal upon these passions : then they became thy virtues and delights . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And though thou wert from the stock of the choleric , or of the voluptuous , or of the religiously frantic , or of the vindictive : At last all thy passions grew virtues , and all thy devils angels . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once thou hadst wild dogs in thy cellar but at last they changed into birds and sweet singers . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Out of thy poisons thou breeds a balsam for thee thou didst milk thy cow of sorrow now thou drinks the sweet milk of its udder . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And from this time forth , nothing evil growth out of thee , unless it be the evil that growth out of the struggle of thy virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brother , if thou hast good luck , thou hast one virtue and no more : thus thou walked more easily over the bridge . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is a distinction to have many virtues , but a hard lot and many having gone to the desert killed themselves , because they were tired of being the battle and battlefield of virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brother , are warfare and battle evil ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But necessary is this evil , necessary are envy and mistrust and among thy virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , how each of thy virtues is covetous for the highest : it longer for thy whole spirit to be its herald , it longer for thy whole power in wrath , love and hatred . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Jealous is each virtue of the other , and a terrible thing is jealousy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even virtues may perish from jealousy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who is encompassed by the flame of jealousy at last , like the scorpion , turned the poisonous sting towards himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , my brother , didst thou never see a virtue backbone and stab itself ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man is a something that must be surpassed : and therefore thou shalt love thy virtues : for thou wilt perish from them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye are not going to slay , ye judges and sacrifices , before the animal hath nodded . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , the pale criminal hath nodded : from his eye there speaker the great contempt . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Mine I is a something that shall be surpassed : for me mine I is the great contempt of man : thus something speaker out of that eye . <end>
<unchecked> <start> His highest moment was when he judged himself : let not the sublime one fall back into his lower state ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is no salvation for him who thus suffered from himself unless it be speedy death . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Your slaying , ye judges , shall be pity and not revenge . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And w T whilst slaying take care to justify life itself ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is not enough that ye should be reconciled unto him whom ye are slaying . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let your sorrow be love unto beyond man : thus ye justify your still living . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Enemy ye shall say , but not wicked one diseased one ye shall say , but not wretch fool ye shall say , but not sinner . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thou , red judge , if thou wert to declare aloud all that thou hast done in thy thoughts , everybody would cry : Away with this filth and worm of poison ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But one thing is thought , another is deed , another is the picture of the deed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The wheel of reason rolled not between them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A picture made this pale man pale . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Of the same growth with himself was his deed when he did it but when it was done , he could not bear the picture of it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He ever saw himself as the doer of one deed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Madness I call that : the exceptional was engrained upon his nature . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The streak of chalk paralysed the hen the stroke he struck paralysed his poor reason . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Madness after the deed I call that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Listen , ye judges ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is , besides , another madness : it is before the deed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , ye did not creep far enough into this soul ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus speaker the red judge : Why did that criminal murder ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> He was going to rob . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I say unto you : his soul asked for blood , not for prey : he was thirsting for the happiness of the knife ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But his poor reason understood not that madness and persuaded him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is blood worth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> it said wouldst not thou at least make a prey along with it ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> take revenge along with it ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And he heartened unto his poor reason : like lead its speech lay upon him , then he robbed when murdering . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He did not like to be ashamed of his madness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And now again lieth the lead of his guilt upon him , and again his poor reason is so chilled , so paralysed , so heavy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If he could but shake his head , that burden would roll off . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But who will shake that head ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is this man ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> A mass of diseases which through the spirit reach out into the world : there they are going to prey . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is this man ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> A coil of wild serpents which seldom are at rest with each other thus singly they depart to search for prey in the world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold this poor body ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What it suffered and longed for , this poor soul interpreted : it interpreted it as a murderous lust and greediness for the happiness of the knife . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who is diseased now is surprised by the evil which is evil now . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He willett to cause pain with what cause pain to him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But there have been other times and another evil and another good . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once doubt and the will unto self were evil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then the diseased became heretics or witches : as heretics or witches they suffered and sought to cause suffering . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This however entered not into your ears it is hurtful unto your good ones , ye say unto me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But what are your good ones worth unto me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many things in your good ones cause loathing unto me not what is evil in them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I even wish they had a madness from which they might perish like this pale criminal . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Indeed I wish their madness could be named truth or faithfulness or justice : but they have their virtue to live long and in a miserable ease . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am a railing alongside the stream whoever is able to seize me , may seize me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Your crutch , however , I am not . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Of all that is written I love only that which the writer wrote with his blood . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Write with blood , and thou wilt learn that blood is spirit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is not easily possible to understand other people s blood . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I hate the reading idlers . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who knower the reader doth nothing more for the reader . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Another century of readers and spirit itself will stink . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That everybody is allowed to learn to read spoiled in the long run not only writing but thinking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once spirit was God , then it became man , and now it is becoming mob . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who written in blood and seemeth not to be read , but to be learnt by heart . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the mountains the shortest way is from summit to summit : but for that thou neediest long legs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Apophthegms shall be summits , and they who are spoken unto , great ones and tall . <end>
<unchecked> <start> spirit full of a gay wickedness : these agree well together . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I desire to have goblins round me , for I am brave . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Courage that dispelled ghosts created goblins for itself , courage desire to laugh . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I no longer feel as ye do : this cloud which I see beneath me , that blackness and heaviness at which I laugh , that is your thunder cloud . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye look upward when longing to be exalted . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And I look downward because I am exalted . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Which of you can at the same time laugh and be exalted ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who stride across the highest mountains laughed at all tragedies whether of the stage or of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Brave , unconcerned , scornful , violent , thus wisdom would have us to be : she is a woman and ever lovett the warrior only . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye say unto me : Life is hard to bear . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But for what purpose have ye got in the morning your pride and in the evening your submission ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Life is hard to bear . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But do not pretend to be so frail ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> We are all good he asses and she asses of burden . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What have we in common with the rose bud that trembled because a drop of dew lieth on its body ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is true : we love life , not because we are accustomed to life , but because we are accustomed to love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is always a madness in love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is , however , also always a reason in madness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And to my thinking as a lover of life , butterflies , soap bubbles , and whatever is of their kind among men , know most of happiness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To see these light , foolish , delicate , mobile little souls flitting about that move Zarathustra to tears and to song . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I could believe only in a God who would know how to dance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when I saw my devil , I found him earnest , thorough , deep , solemn : he was the spirit of gravity , through him all things fall . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not through wrath but through laughter one slayer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Arise ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> let us slay the spirit of gravity ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I learned to walk : now I let myself run . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I learned to fly : now I need no pushing to move me from the spot . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now I am light , now I fly , now I see myself beneath myself , now a God dance through me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra s eye had seen that a young man avoided him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And one night when walking alone through the hills round about the town that is called the Cow of Many Colours : behold , walking there he found that young man sitting with his back against a tree and gazing into the valley with a tired look . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra taking hold of the tree against which the young man was sitting spake thus : If I wished to shake this tree with my hands I could not do so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the wind which we do not see tormented and beneath it wherever is listen . <end>
<unchecked> <start> By unseen hands we are bent and tormented worst . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Astonished the young man rose and said : I hear Zarathustra and was just thinking of him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra answered : Wherefore dost thou fear ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is with man as with the tree . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The more he would ascend to height and light the stronger are his roots striving northwards , downwards , into the dark , the deep , the evil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ay , towards the evil ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> cried the youth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How was it possible for thee to discover my soul ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra said smiling : Some souls will never be discovered , unless they be invented first . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou sadist the truth , Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I do not trust myself any longer since I am striving upwards , neither doth anybody else trust me say , how is that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I alter too quickly : my to day refute my yesterday . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I frequently overlap steps when I ascend no step pardoned me for that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When I reach the summit I always find myself alone . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nobody speaker unto me , the frost of solitude maketh me tremble . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What do I seek on high ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> My contempt and longing grow together the higher I ascend the more I despise him who ascended . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What seemeth he on high ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> How ashamed I am of mine ascending and stumbling ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How I mock at my vehement panting and puffing ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How I hate him who lieth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How tired I am on high ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Here the youth was silent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And Zarathustra contemplating the tree by which they stood spake thus : This tree standish lonely by the mountains it grew high beyond man and animal . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if it were to speak it would have nobody to understand it : so high hath it grown . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now , it is waiting and waiting , for what is it waiting , say ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> It dwellers too close to the clouds : It is waiting I suppose for the first lightning ? <end>

<unchecked> <start> It was for my , destruction that I longed when I was striving upwards , and thou art the lightning I waited for ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , what am I since thou hast appeared unto us ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is the envy of thee which hath destroyed me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Speaking thus the youth wept bitterly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra , however , put his arm round him and led him away with him . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Weary with watching thou art made by thy seeking , and much too wakeful . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Towards the free height thou art striving , for stars thy soul is thirsting . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Much of prison and mould is still left in him : his eye needed to be purified . <end>

<unchecked> <start> But by my love and hope I conjure thee : throw not away thy love and hope ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Noble thou feels thyself , and that thou art noble feel even the others who are angry with thee and cast evil glances . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Know that a noble one is in the way of all . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A noble one is in the way of the good : and even if they call him a good one , by so doing they seek to put him aside . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The noble one wished to create something new and a new virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The good one willett that old things should be preserved . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But that is not the danger of the noble one , to become a good one , but to become an insolent , a sneering one , a destroyer . <end>

<unchecked> <start> And then they slandered all high hopes . <end>

<unchecked> <start> But by my love and hope I conjure thee : throw not away the hero in thy soul ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Keep holy thy highest hope ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> There are preachers of death , and the earth is full of those unto whom it is necessary to preach the abandonment of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Full is earth of superfluous ones , spoiled is life by the much too many . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would they could be tempted away from this life by eternal life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Yellow ones the preachers of death are called or black ones . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I shall , however , show them unto you in other colours besides . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There are the terrible who carry about within themselves a beast of prey and have no choice except voluptuousness or self laceration . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And even their voluptuousness is self laceration . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They have not even become human beings , these terrible ones : let them preach abandonment of life and themselves pass away ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> There are the consumptive of soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When scarce born they begin to die and long for the doctrine of weariness and renunciation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They would fain be dead , and we should approve of their will ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us beware lest we awaken these dead ones or damage these living coffins ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> But only they themselves are refuted and their eye that teeth only that one face of existence . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wrapped in thick melancholy and hungry for those little accidents which produce death they wait with clenched teeth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or : they reach out for sweetmeats and so doing mock their own childishness : they cling to the straw of their life and mock because they are hanging on a straw . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Their wisdom is : A fool he who remained alive but to that extent we are fools ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And that is the greatest folly of life ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Life is but suffering others say , and they do not lie . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Well then , see that you die ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> See to it that life which is but suffering come to an end . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And let this be the teaching of your virtue : Thou shalt kill thyself ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> thou shalt steal thyself away ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lust is sin , the preachers of death say let us turn aside and produce no children ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Giving birth is noisome say the others Why give birth ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> One giveth birth to unhappy ones only ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And they also are preachers of death . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Pity is needed a third section say . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Accept from me whatever I have ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Accept from me whatever I am . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The less am I bound unto life ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Were they piteous at heart , they would set the minds of their neighbours against life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To be evil that would be their proper goodness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They yearn to be rid of life : what care they it with their chains and gifts they tie others the faster ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye also to whom life is scornful labour and unrest : are ye not wearied of life ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Are ye not ripe for the sermon of death ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> All of you to whom scornful labour is dear , and what is swift , what is new and what is strange are dear , ye bear yourselves ill your industry is retreat and will to forget itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If ye had more belief in life ye would yield yourselves the less to the moment . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But ye have not enough substance within you to enable you to wait , not even to idle . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Or : eternal life : that is the same unto me , if they only pass away quickly ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> We like neither to be spared by our best enemies , nor by those whom we love from our heart of heart . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let me tell you the truth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brethren in war ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love you from my heart s heart . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am and was your like . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And , besides , I am your best enemy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore let me tell you the truth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I know the hatred and envy of your heart . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye are not great enough not to know hatred and envy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then be great enough not to be ashamed of them ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if ye cannon be saints of knowledge , at least be its warriors . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are the companions and pioneers of the saints holiness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I see many soldiers : would I could see many warriors ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> I do not advise you to conclude peace , but to conquer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let your work be a fight , your peace a victory ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> One cannon be silent and sit still unless one hath bow and arrow . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Otherwise one taketh and quarrelled . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let your peace be a victory ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye say , a good cause will allow even war ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I say unto you : a good war hallowed every cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> War and courage have done more great things than charity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not your pity , but your bravery , hath hitherto saved those who had met with an accident . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is good ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> ye ask . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To be brave is good . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let the little girlies talk : To be good is what is sweet and touching at the same time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They call you heartless : but your heart is genuine , and I love the shame of your heartiness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye are ashamed of your flood tide , and others are ashamed of their ebb . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye are ugly ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Well then , my brethren ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wrap the sublime round yourselves , the mantle of what is ugly ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when your soul warmth great it warmth haughty , and in your sublimity there is wickedness . <end>

<unchecked> <start> In wickedness the haughty one and the weakling meet . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But they misunderstand each other . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I know you . <end>
