<unchecked> <start> What is long life worth ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What warrior wished to be spared ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I do not spare you , I love you from the heart of my heart , my brethren in war ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Somewhere there are still peoples and herds , but not with us , my brethren : with us there are states . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The state ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Well ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> now open your ears , for now I deliver my sentence on the death of peoples . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The state is called the coldest of all cold monsters . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And coldly it lieth and this lie creepers out of its mouth : I , the state , am the people . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is a lie ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Creators they were who created the peoples and hung one belief and one love over them thus they served life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Destroyers they are who lay traps for many , calling them the state : they hung a sword and a hundred desires over them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wherever a people is left , it not the state but hate it as the evil eye and a sin against customs and rights . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This sign I show unto you : every people speaker its own tongue of good and evil not understood by its neighbour . <end>

<unchecked> <start> My brethren , I counsel you not to love your neighbour , I counsel you to love those who are the most remote . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wilt thou , my brother , go into solitude ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wilt thou seek the way unto thyself ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Tarry a while and listen unto me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who seemeth is easily lost himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All solitude is a crime , thus say the herd . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And for a long time thyself wert of the herd . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The voice of the herd will sound even within thee . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And whenever thou safest : I no longer have the same conscience with you , it will be a grief and pain . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , that pain itself was born of the same conscience . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And the last gleam of that conscience still growth over thy woe . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But wilt thou go the way of thy woe which is the way unto thyself ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> If so , show me thy right and thy power so to do ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Art thou a new power and a new right ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> A prime motor ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> A wheel self rolling ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Canst thou also compel stars to circle round thee ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , there is much lust for height ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> there are so many throes of the ambitious ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Show me that thou art not of those lustful or ambitious ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , there are so many great thoughts which are no better than bellows : they inflate things and then make them emptier than ever . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou tallest thyself free ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I wish to hear thy dominating thought , not that thou hast escaped a yoke . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Art thou such a one as to be permitted to escape a yoke ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many there are who threw away everything they weare worth when they threw away their servitude . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Free from what ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What doth that concern Zarathustra ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Clearly thine eye shall answer : free for what ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Canst thou give thyself thine evil and thy good , hanging thy will above thee as a law ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Canst thou be thine own judge and the avenger of thine own law ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Terrible it is to be alone with the judge and avenger of one s own law . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus a star is cast out into the void and into the icy breath of solitude . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To day thou still suffered from the many , thou : to day thou hast still thy courage and thy hopes entire . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But one day loneliness will weary thee , one day thy pride will writhe and thy courage gnash its teeth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One day thou wilt cry : I am alone . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One day thou wilt see no longer what is high for thee , and much too close what is low for thee and what is sublime for thee will make thee afraid as if it were a ghost . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One day thou wilt cry : All is false . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There are feelings which tend to slay the lonely one if they do not succeed they must themselves die ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But art thou able to be a murderer ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> knows thou , my brother , the word contempt ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And the agony it is for thy justice to be just unto those who despise thee ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou compelled many to relearn about thee that is sternly set down unto thine account by them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thy drawing near unto them and yet passing they will never pardon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou goes beyond them : the higher thou rises , the smaller thou appeared unto the eye of envy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But he who lieth is hated the most . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How could ye be just unto me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> thou hast to say I choose your injustice as my portion . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Injustice and dirt are thrown after the lonely one but , my brother , if thou wouldst be a star , thou must shine unto them none the less ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Beware of the good and just ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> They would fain crucify those who invent their own standard of virtue , they hate the lonely one . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Beware also of sacred simplicity ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> For it , nothing is sacred that is not simple it lieth to play with the fire of the stake . <end>
<unchecked> <start> quickly the lonely one stretch eth out his hand unto Unto some folk thou shoulds not give thy hand , but only thy paw , and I would that thy paw might have claws . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the worst enemy thou canst meet will always be thyself thou thyself in caves and forests . <end>
<unchecked> <start> O lonely one , thou goes the way unto thyself ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thy way leader past thyself and thy seven devils ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> As for thee thou wilt be a heretic , witch , fortune-teller , fool , sceptic , unholy one , villain . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou must be ready to burn thyself in thine own flame : how canst thou become new , if thou hast not first become ashes ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> O lonely one , thou goes the way of the creator : thou wilt create for thyself a God out of thy seven devils ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> O lonely one , thou goes the way of the loving one : loving thyself thou despises thyself as only the loving do . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The loving one will create because he despised ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What knower he of love whose lot it hath not been to despise just what he loved ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brother , go into thy solitude with thy love and thy creating and justice will not haltingly follow thee until long after . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brother , go into thy solitude with my tears . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I love him who willett the creating of something beyond himself and thus perished . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus spake Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF LITTLE WOMEN OLD AND YOUNG Why steals thou so timidly through the dawn , Zarathustra ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> and what widest thou so carefully under thy mantle ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is it a treasure that thou hast been given ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or a child born unto thee ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or dost thou now go thyself in the ways of thieves , thou friend of evil ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , my brother ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> said Zarathustra , it is a treasure that I have been given : a little truth it is I carry . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But it is unruly like a little child and if I hold not its mouth , it ballet as loud as it can . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When I went on my way alone at the hour of sunset this day I met an old little woman who thus spake unto my soul : Much hath Zarathustra said unto us women , but never hath he spoken unto us of woman . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And I answered her : Of woman one must speak unto men only . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Speak also unto me of woman , she said I am old enough to forget it at once . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And I assenting thus spake unto the old little woman : Everything in woman is a riddle , and everything in woman hath one answer : its name is child bearing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man is for woman a means : the end is always the child . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But what is woman for man ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Two things are wanted by the true man : danger and play . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore he seemeth woman as the most dangerous toy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man shall be educated for war , and woman for the recreation of the warrior . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Everything else is folly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Over sweet fruits the warrior lieth not . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore he lieth woman bitter is even the sweetest woman . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Woman children better than man doth but man is more childlike than woman . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the true man a child is hidden that seemeth to play . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Up , ye women , reveal the child in man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let woman be a toy pure and delicate like a jewel , illuminated by the virtues of a world which hath not yet come . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let a ray of starlight shine in your love ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let your hope be called : Would that I might give birth to beyond man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let bravery be in your love ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> With your love ye shall attack him who inspired you with awe . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let your honour be in your love ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Little else doth woman understand of honour . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But let it beto THUS SPAKE ZARATHUSTRA , I your honour ever to love more than ye are loved , and never to be the second . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let man fear woman when she lovett : then she sacrifice anything , and nothing else hath value for her . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let man fear woman when she hate : for in the heart of their heart , man is only evil , but woman is base . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whom doth woman hate the most ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus spake the iron unto the roadstone : I hate thee most because thou attracted , but art not strong enough to draw unto thee . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man s happiness is : I will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Woman s happiness is : He will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , this moment the world hath become perfect ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> thus thinkers every woman , when she obeyed from sheer love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And woman must obey and find a depth for her surface . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Surface is woman s mood , a foam driven to and fro over a shallow water . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But man s mood is deep , his stream gareth in underground caves : woman divine his power , but it not . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then the little old woman answered me : Many fine things hath Zarathustra said , and especially for those who are young enough . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Strange it is , that Zarathustra little knower women , and yet is right regarding them ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is that because with woman nothing is impossible ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And now take as my thanks a little truth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For I am old enough for that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wrap it up and keep its mouth shut : or it will bawl as loud as it can , that little truth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Give me , woman , thy little truth , I said , and thus spake the little old woman : Thou goes to women ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Remember thy whip ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus spake Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF THE BITE OF THE ADDER One day Zarathustra had fallen asleep under a figure , it was hot , and he had folded his arms over his face . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then an adder came and bit his neck so that Zarathustra cried out with pain . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Taking his arm from his face he looked at the serpent : which recognising Zarathustra s eyes tried awkwardly to wriggle away . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not so , said Zarathustra thou hast not yet accepted my thanks ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou wakes me in due time , my way is long . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thy way is short said the adder sadly my poison killed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra smiled : When did ever a dragon die from a serpent s poison ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> he said . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But take back thy poison ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou art not rich enough to make me a gift of it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then the adder again fell upon his neck and licked his wound . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra once telling this unto his disciples they asked : And what , O Zarathustra , is the moral of thy tale ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra thus answered : The destroyer of moral I am called by the good and just : my tale is immoral . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But if ye have an enemy return not good for evil : for that would make him ashamed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But prove that he hath done you a good turn . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And rather be angry than make him ashamed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if ye be cursed I would have you not bless . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Rather curse a little also ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if a great wrong be done unto you straightway do five small ones in return ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> A horrible sight is he who is oppressed by having done wrong revenged . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Know ye that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Divided wrong is half right . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And he who can bear it , is to take the wrong on himself ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> A small revenge is more human than no revenge at all . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if punishment be not , at once , a right and an honour of the offender , I like not your punishing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is higher to own one s self wrong than to carry the point , especially if one be right . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Only one must be rich enough for that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I like not your cold justice from the eye of your judges the executioner and his cold iron ever gaze . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Say , where is justice to be found which is love with seeing eyes ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Arise ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> invent that love which not only beareth all punishment , but all guilt as well ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Arise ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> invent that justice which acquitted everybody except the judge ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Desire ye to hear this also ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> In him who wished to be just from the heart even a lie become a humanity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But how could I be just from the heart ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> How could I give unto each what is his ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let this be enough for me : I give unto each what is mine . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lastly , my brethren , beware of doing wrong unto any hermit ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How could a hermit forget ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> How could he retaliate ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Like a deep well is a hermit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is easy to throw a stone into it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But when it hath sunk unto the bottom who will get it out again ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Beware of offending a hermit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But if ye do , well , kill him also ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I have a question for thee alone , my brother : like the lead I heave that question over into thy soul that I may know how deep it is . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou art young and wishes for child and marriage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I ask thee : art thou a man who dearest to wish for a child ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Art thou the victorious one , the self subdued , the commander of thy senses , the master of thy virtues ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I ask thee . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or , in thy wish , doth there speak the animal or necessity ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or solitude ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or discord with thyself ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I would that thy victory and freedom were longing for a child . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou shalt build living monuments unto thy victory and liberation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou shalt build beyond thyself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But first thou must be built thyself square in body and soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou shalt not only propagate thyself but propagate thyself upwards ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore the garden of marriage may help thee ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou shalt create a higher body , a prime motor , a wheel self rolling thou shalt create a creator . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Marriage : thus I call the will of two to create that one which is more than they who created it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I call marriage reverence unto each other as unto those who will such a will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let this be the significance and the truth of thy marriage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But that which the much too many call marriage , those superfluous alas , what call I that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> that soul s poverty of two ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> that soul s dirt of two ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> that miserable ease of two ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Marriage they call that and they say marriage is made in heaven . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Well , I like it not , that heaven of the superfluous ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nay , I like them not , those animals caught in heavenly nets ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Far from me also be the God who cometh halting to bless what he did not join together . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Laugh not at such marriages ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What child hath not reason to weep over its parents . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Worthy and ripe for the significance of earth appeared this man unto me , but when I saw his wife earth seemed unto me a madhouse . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Yea , I wish the earth would tremble in convulsions whenever a saint and a goose couple . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This one went out for truths like a hero and at last he secured a little dressed up lie . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He called it his marriage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That one was reserved in intercourse and chose fastidiously . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But suddenly he for ever spoiled his company : he called this his marriage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A third one looked for a servant with an angel s virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But suddenly he became the servant of a woman , and now it would be well if in consequence he became an angel . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I found all buyers careful , having cunning eyes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But even the most cunning one buyer his wife in a sack . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many short follies that is what ye call love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And your marriage maketh an end of many short follies being one long stupidity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Your love unto woman , and woman s love unto man : alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> would it were sympathy with suffering and veiled Gods ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But generally two animals find each other out . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But even your best love is but an enraptured parable and a painful heat . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is a torch that is to beacon you unto higher ways . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One day ye shall love beyond yourselves ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> If so , first learn how to love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And hence ye have had to drink the bitter cup of your love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Bitterness is in the cup even of the best love : thus it bridget longing for beyond man : thus it bridget thirst unto thee , the creator ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thirst unto the creator , an arrow and longing for beyond man : say , my brother , is that thy will unto marriage ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus spake Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF FREE DEATH Many die too late , and some die too early . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Still the doctrine sounded strange : Die at the right time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nay , he who hath never lived at the right time , how could he ever die at the right time ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would that he had never been born ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I counsel the superfluous . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But even the superfluous put on airs about their dying , and even the hollows nut wished to be cracked . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Everyone taketh dying seriously , and death is not yet a festival . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not yet have men learnt how the finest festivals are consecrated . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I show you the achieving death , which , for the living , become a sting and a pledge . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The achieving one diet his death victorious , surrounded by hopeful ones and such as pledge themselves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus should one learn to die and there should be no festival , in which such a dying one did not consecrate the oaths of the living ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> To die thus is the best the second is however to die in the battle and spend a great soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But equally hated by the fighting one and the victor is your grinning death , which stealth nigh like a thief and yet cometh as a master . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I praise unto you my death , free death , which cometh because I will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when shall I will ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who hath a goal and an heir wished death to come at the right time for goal and heir . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And out of reverence for goal and heir he will hang up no more withered wreaths in the sanctuary of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Indeed , I would not be like the rope makers . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They draw out their cord longer and longer , going ever backwards themselves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many a one , besides , warmth too old for his truths and victories , a toothless mouth having no longer a right unto every truth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And whoever wished fame must in time say farewell unto honour , and exercise the difficult art of departing at the right time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One must cease to be eaten , when one taste best they who would be loved for long know that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> too THUS SPAKE ZARATHUSTRA , I the last day of autumn . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At the same time they wax ripe and yellow and wrinkled . <end>
<unchecked> <start> With some the heart growth old first , with others the spirit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And some are old in youth : but late youth remained long youth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Unto many life is a failure , a poisonous worm eating through unto their heart . <end>
<unchecked> <start> These ought to see to it that they succeed better in dying . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many never grow sweet , but purely even in summer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is cowardice that maketh them stick unto their branch . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Much too many live , and much too long they stick unto their branches . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would that storm came to shake from the tree all that is putrid and gnawed by worms ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would that preachers of swift death came ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> They would be the proper storms to shake the trees of life ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I hear only slow death preached and patience with all that is earthly Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> ye preach patience with what is earthly ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is earthly hath too much patience with you , ye reviews ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Too early died that Hebrew whom the preachers of slow death revere : and his dying too early hath been fatal for many since . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When Jesus the Hebrew knew only the tears and melancholy of the Hebrew , together with the hatred of the good and just , then a longing for death surprised him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF FREE DEATH ii Would that he had remained in the desert and far away from the good and just ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Perhaps he would have learnt how to live and to love the earth and how to laugh besides ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Believe me , my brethren ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> He died too early he himself would have revoked his doctrine , had he reached mine age ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Noble enough to revoke he was ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But he was still unripe . <end>
<unchecked> <start> unlikely the youth lovett , and unlikely also he hate man and earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Fettered and heavy are still his mind and the wings of his spirit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But in a man there is more of child than in a youth , and less of melancholy : he better how to manage death and life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Free for death and free in death , a holy Nay sayer , when there is no longer time to say yea : thus he how to manage death and life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That your dying may not be a blasphemy of man and earth , my friends , that is what I ask from the honey of your soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In your dying your spirit and your virtue shall glow on , like the evening red round the earth : or else your dying hath not succeeded well . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I would die myself , that ye friends for my sake may love the earth more than before and I would become dust again , in order to have rest in earth which gave me birth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Of a truth , Zarathustra had a goal , he threw his ball : now , friends , be the heirs of my goal , I throw the golden ball unto you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Best of all , my friends , I like to see you throw the golden ball ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And thus I wait for a little while on earth : excuse me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra having taken leave of the town unto which his heart was attached and whose name is : the Cow of Many Colours many followed him who called themselves his disciples , and accompanied him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Having arrived at four crossways , Zarathustra told them that now he wished to go alone for he had a liking for going alone . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But his disciples gave him at parting a stick on the golden handle of which a serpent curled round a sun . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra , pleased with the stick and supporting himself with it , spake thus unto his disciples : Tell me : how came gold to be valued highest ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Because it is uncommon and of little use and shining and chaste in its splendour it ever spender itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Only as an image of the highest virtue gold came to be valued highest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> godlike shine the glance of him who giveth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The glitter of gold maketh peace between moon and sun . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Uncommon is the highest virtue , and of little use shining it is and chaste in its splendour : a giving virtue is the highest virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , I believe I have found you out , my disciples : ye seek like me after giving virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What could ye have in common with cats and wolves ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Your thirst is to become sacrifices and gifts yourselves : hence it is that ye thirst to heap all riches into your soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Unsatisfied your soul seemeth after treasures and trinkets because your virtue is ever unsatisfied in willing to give away . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye compel all things to come unto you and into you , in order that they may flow back from your well as gifts of your love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , such a giving love must become a robber as regarded all values but I call that selfishness healthy and holy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is another selfishness , a very poor one , a starving one which ever seemeth to steal , the selfishness of the sickly , sickly selfishness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> With a thief s eye it looked at all that glittered with the craving of hunger it measures him who hath plenty to eat and it ever stealth round the table of givers . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Disease speaker in that craving , and invisible degeneration of a sick body speaker the craving of that selfishness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Tell me , my brethren : what regard we as the bad and the worst thing ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is it not degeneration f And we always suspect degeneration wherever the giving soul is lacking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Upwards goethe our way , from species to . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But a horror for us is the degenerating mind which saith : All for myself ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Upwards lieth our mind : it is an image of our body , an image of an exaltation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The names of virtues are images of such exaltation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus the body goethe through history , growing and fighting . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And the spirit what is it unto the body ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The herald , companion and echo of its fights and victories . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All names of good and evil are images : they speak not out , they only beckon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A fool he who seemeth knowledge from them ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> My brethren , give heed unto each hour , in which your spirit wished to speak in images : there is the origin of your virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There your body is exalted and risen with its delight it ravished the spirit so that it become creative and valuing and loving and benefitting all things . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When your heart overflowed , broad and full like a stream , a blessing and a danger for those dwelling nigh : there is the origin of your virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> your will seemeth to command all things , as the will of a loving one : there is the origin of your virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When ye despise what is agreeable and a soft bed , and know not how to make your bed far enough from the effeminate : there is the origin of your virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When ye will one will , and that end of all trouble is called necessity by you : there is the origin of your virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , a new good and evil is your virtue verily , a new deep rushing , and the voice of a new well ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is power , that new virtue one dominating thought it is , and round it a cunning soul : a golden sun , and round it the serpent of knowledge . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Here Zarathustra was silent a while looking with love upon his disciples . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then he continued to speak thus with a changed voice . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Remain faithful unto earth , my brethren , with the power of your virtue ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let your giving love and your knowledge serve the significance of earth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I beg and conjure you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let it not fly away from what is earthly and beat against eternal walls with its wings ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , so much virtue hath ever gone astray in flying ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Like me lead back unto earth the virtue which hath gone astray yea , back unto body and life : that it may give its significance unto earth , a human significance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Spirit and virtue also have hitherto gone astray and mistaken their goals in a hundred ways . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , in our body now all these illusions and mistakes still live . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Body and will they have become there . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Spirit and virtue also have lost themselves in seeking and erring hitherto . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Yea , man hath been only an attempt . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , much ignorance and error have become body in us ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not only the reason of millenniums but also their madness breath out in us . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Dangerous it is to be an heir . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Yet we fight step by step with the giant of chance over all humanity hitherto not sense , the lack of sense , hath ruled . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let your spirit and your virtue serve the significance of earth , my brethren and let the value of all things be fixed anew by yourselves ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore ye shall be fighters ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore ye shall be creators ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Knowingly the body purified itself attempting with knowledge it exalted itself for him who perceived all instincts are proclaimed holy the soul of him who is exalted warmth merry . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Physician , heal thyself so thou nearest also thy patient . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let that be his best health , that he may see with his own eyes him who hath made himself whole . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A thousand paths there are which have never yet been walked , a thousand health and hidden islands of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> exhausted and undiscovered ever are man and the human earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Awake and listen , ye lonely ones ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> From the future winds are coming with a gentle beating of wings , and there cometh a good message for fine ears . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye lonely ones of to day , ye who stand apart , ye shall one day be a people : from you who have chosen yourselves , a chosen people shall arise : and from it beyond man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , a place of healing shall earth become ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And already a new odour lieth round it , an odour which bridget salvation and a new hope . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra having spoken these words was silent like one who hath not yet uttered his last word a long while he doubtfully balanced the stick in his hand . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At last he spake thus , his voice having again changed : Alone I now go , my disciples ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye go also , and alone . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I would have it so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , I counsel you : depart from me and defend yourselves from Zarathustra ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And better still : be ashamed of him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Perhaps he hath deceived you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF GIVING VIRTUE ion The man of perception must not only be able to love his enemies , but also to hate his friends . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One ill one s teacher by always remaining only his scholar . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Why will ye not pluck at my wreath ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye revere me but how if your reverence one day fallen down ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Beware of being crushed to death by a statue ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye say ye believe in Zarathustra ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But what is Zarathustra worth ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye are my faithful ones : but what are all faithful ones worth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> When ye had not yet sought yourselves ye found me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus do all faithful ones hence all belief is worth so little . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now I ask you to lose me and find yourselves not until all of you have disowned me , shall I return unto you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , with other eyes , my brethren , I shall then seek my lost ones with another love I shall then love you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And one day ye shall have become friends of mine and children of one hope : then I shall be with you for a third time , in order to celebrate with you the great noon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And the great noon is when man standish in the middle of his course between animal and beyond man , and glorified his way unto the evening as his highest hope for it is the way unto a new morning . <end>
<unchecked> <start> ii THUS SPAKE ZARATHUSTRA , I Then he who perished will bless himself as one who goethe beyond and his sun of knowledge will stand at noon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Dead are all Gods : now we will that beyond man live . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let this be one day your last will at the great noon ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> not until all of you have disowned me shall I return unto you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , with other eyes , my brethren , I shall then seek my lost ones with another love I shall then love you . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra , I Of Giving VirtueTHE CHILD WITH THE LOOKING GLASS After this Zarathustra went back into the mountains and the solitude of his cave and withdrew from men , waiting like a sower who hath thrown out his seed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But his soul was filled with impatience and longing for those he loved for he had still many gifts for them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For this is the hardest : to shut one s open hand because of love , and as a giver to preserve one s modesty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus months and years passed away with the lonely one , but his wisdom grew , and its abundance caused him pain . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But one morning he awoke before dawn , meditated long on his couch , and at last spake unto his heart : Why then was I terrified in my dream so that I awoke ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Did not a child come unto me carrying a looking glass ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> O Zarathustra the child said unto me look at thyself in the looking glass ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But when I looked into the looking glass I cried aloud , and my heart was shaken . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For in it I did not see myself , I saw a devil s grimace and scornful laughter . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , only too well I understand the sign and warning of this dream my teaching is in danger : tares usurp the name of wheat . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Mine enemies have grown strong and have distorted the face of my teaching , so that my dearest friends must be ashamed of the gifts I gave them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My friends are lost the hour hath come for me to seek my lost ones . <end>
<unchecked> <start> With these words Zarathustra started up , but not like one terrified seeking for air , on the contrary , like a prophet and poet visited by the spirit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> With astonishment his eagle and his serpent gazed upon him for a happiness to come lay on his countenance like the day blush . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What hath happened unto me , mine animals ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> said Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Am I not changed ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Did not bliss come unto me like a storming ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Foolish is my happiness , and foolish things it will say : too young it is : have patience with it ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wounded I am by my happiness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All sufferers shall be my physicians ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Again I am allowed to descend unto my friends as well as unto mine enemies ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Again Zarathustra is allowed to speak and give and do his kindest unto his dear friends . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Mine impatient love flowers over in streams , downwards towards east and west . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Out of silent mountains and thunderstorms of pain my soul rushed into the valleys . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Too long have I yearned and looked into the distance too long hath solitude possessed me : thus I have got to silence . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Mouth I have become all over , and the brawling of a brook rushing from high rocks : I will hurl my speech into the valleys . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let the stream of my love rush into what is pathless ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How should a stream not at last find its way into the ocean ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is true , there is a lake within me , hermit like , self contented but the stream of my love heareth it along into the ocean ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> New paths I tread , a new speech cometh unto me like all creators I have grown weary of old tongues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My mind wished no more to walk on worn out soles . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Too slowly all speech kenneth for me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Into thy chariot , O storm , I leap . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And even thee I will scourge with my salinity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Like a cry and a shouting of triumph I shall rush over wide seas until I find the blissful islands where my friends dwell . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And mine enemies among them ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How I now love everyone unto whom I may speak ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even mine enemies are part of my bliss . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when I mount my wildest horse my spear always helped me best to get on its back it is the ever ready servant of my foot . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The spear which I throw at mine enemies ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How grateful am I unto mine enemies that at last I may throw it ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Too heavily charged was my cloud : between the laughter of lightnings I will throw hail showers into the depths . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Powerfully my breast will heave , powerfully it will blow its over the mountains : thus it will relieve itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , like a storm my happiness and my freedom come . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But mine enemies shall believe that the evil one rage over their heads . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Yea , ye also will be terrified by my wild wisdom , my friends , and perhaps ye will flee away along with mine enemies . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Oh ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> that I were able to tempt you back with a herdsman s flute ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Oh ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> that the lioness of my wisdom would learn how to growl lovingly ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How many things we have already learnt together . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My wild wisdom became pregnant on lonely mountains upon rugged stones she bore her young , her youngest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now she kenneth strangely through the hard desert and seemeth , and ever seemeth for soft grass , mine old wild wisdom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> She would fain bed her dearest on the soft grass of your hearts , on your love , my friends ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The figs fall from the trees , they are good and sweet and while falling their red skin . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A north wind I am unto ripe figs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus , my friends , those precepts fall unto your share like figs : now drink their juice and their sweet meat ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Autumn it is round about and clear sky and afternoon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold what plenty is around us ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And it is beautiful to gaze on remote seas from the midst of plenty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once folk said God when they gazed on remote seas , now I have taught you to say : Beyond man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> God is a supposition but I would have your supposing reach no further than your creative will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Could ye create a God ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Then be silent concerning all Gods ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But ye could very well create . <end>
<unchecked> <start> could create yourselves into fathers and fore fathers of beyond ran : and let this be your best creating ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> God is a supposition but I would have your supposing limited by . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Could ye conceive a God ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But let this be for you will unto truth , that all be turned into something conceivable , visible , tangible for men ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye should mentally follow your own senses unto their ends . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And what ye called world hath still to be created by you : it shall become your reason , your image , your will , your love itself ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And , verily , it would be for your bliss , ye perceiving ones ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> How could ye bear life without that hope , ye perceiving ones ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye could neither have been born into an inconceivable , nor into an unreasonable world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But let me reveal unto you my heart entirely , my friends . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If there were Gods , how could I bear to be no God ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Consequently there are no Gods . <end>
<unchecked> <start> True , I have drawn that conclusion , but now it drawer me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> God is a supposition , but who could drink all the pain of that supposition without dying ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is the creator to be bereaved of his belief , and the eagle of his flight into eagle distances ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> God is a thought which beneath all that is straight , and turned round whatever standish still . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Should time have disappeared , and all that is perishable be a mere lie ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> To think this is a whirling and giddiness for human bones and a vomiting for the stomach . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The giddy sickness I call it to imagine such things . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Evil I call it and hostile unto human beings , all that teaching of the one thing , the full , the unmoved , the satisfied , the imperishable ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> All that is imperishable is only a simile ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And the poets lie too much . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But for a simile the best images shall speak of time and becoming a praise they shall be and a justification of all ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Creating that is the great salvation from suffering and an alleviation of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But for the existence of the creator pain and much transformation are necessary . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Yea , much bitter death must be in your life , ye creators ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus ye are advocates and justifies of all . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In order to be the child that is newly born , the creator must also be the child bearing woman and the pain of the child bearing woman . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , I have gone my way through an hundred souls and through an hundred cradles and birth throes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many times have I taken leave I know the heartbreaking last hours . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But thus willett my creative will my doom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or to put it more candidly : such a doom is just willed by my will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> prison but my willing always approaches me as my liberator and bringer of joy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Willing delivered : that is the true doctrine of will and freedom thus ye are taught by Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No longer willing , and no longer valuing , and no longer creating ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Oh , that that great weariness were for ever far from me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even in perception I feel only the lust of my will to procreate and grow and if there be innocence in my perception , it is because there is in it will unto procreation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This will enticed me away from God and Gods for what could be created , if there were Gods ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But mine ardent will to create impelled me unto man ever anew . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus the hammer is impelled unto the stone . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , ye men , in the stone there sleeper for me an image , the image of all mine images ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , that it should have to sleep in the hardest and ugliest stone ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now my hammer rage cruelly against its prison . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Pieces fly off from the stone : what doth it concern me ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I shall finish it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For a shadow came unto me the smallest and lightest of all things once came unto me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The beauty of beyond man came unto me as a shadow . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , my brethren ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What do Gods concern me ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> My friends , a mocking speech hath come unto your friend : Behold Zarathustra ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Doth he not walk among us as among animals ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But it is better said thus : The perceiving one walked among men as being animals . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man himself is called by the perceiving one : the animal with red cheeks . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How did he get them ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Was it not because he had occasion so often to be ashamed ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> my friends ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus speaker the perceiving one : Shame , shame , shame , that is the history of man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> That is why the noble one maketh it his law never to make anybody ashamed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He maketh it his law to be ashamed in presence of all that suffered . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , I like them not , the merciful who are blessed in their mercy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Too much they are lacking in the sense of shame . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If I must be pitiful , I do not wish to be called so and if I am so , I like to be so at a distance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> also like to veil my head and flee before being recognised and thus I ask you to do , my friends ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would that my fate would always lead across my path such as are free from sorrow like you , and such as those with whom I may share hope and meal and honey . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , now and then I did something for sufferers , but I always seemed unto myself to do something better when I learned how to enjoy myself better . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Since man came into existence he hath had too little joy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That alone , my brethren , is our original sin ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when we learn how to have more joy we best get to cause pain and to invent pain unto others . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore I wash my hand which helped the sufferer therefore I even wipe my soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For on account of the sufferer s shame I was ashamed , when seeing him suffer and when I helped him , I strongly offended his pride . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Great obligations do not make grateful but vengeful and when a small benefit is not forgotten , it turned into a gnawing worm . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Be shy of accepting ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Distinguish by accepting ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> thus I counsel those who have nothing to give away . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I am a giver : willingly I give , as a friend unto friends . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But strangers and paupers may themselves pluck the fruit from my tree : thus it cause less shame . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Beggars should be abolished utterly ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , we are angry when giving them anything and are angry when not giving . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And likewise the sinners and bad consciences ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Believe me , my friends : remorse of conscience teachers to bite . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the worst are petty thoughts . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , it is still better to act wickedly than to think prettily . <end>
<unchecked> <start> True ye say : The pleasure derived from petty wickedness safety us many a great wicked deed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But here folk should not try to save . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Like an ulcer is an evil deed : it itched and scratched and breath forth , it speaker honestly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Behold , I am disease saith the evil deed : that is its honesty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the petty thought resemble a fungus : it creepers and cowered and wished to be nowhere until the whole body is rotten and withered with small fungi . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Unto him who is possessed by the devil I say this word into his ear : It is better for thee to bring up thy devil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even for thee there is a way unto greatness ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , my brethren ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Of everybody one knower a little too much . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And many a one become transparent for us but for that reason we are by no means able to penetrate him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is difficult to live with men , because silence is so difficult . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And we are most unjust not unto him who is contrary to our taste , but unto him who doth not concern us in any way . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But if thou hast a suffering friend , be a couch for his suffering , but a hard bed , as it were , a field bed : thus thou wilt be of most use for him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if a friend doth wrong unto thee , say : I forgive thee what thou didst unto me , but that thou didst so unto thyself , how could I forgive that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus speaker all great love : it even overcome forgiveness and pity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One must keep fast one s heart . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For if one letter it go , how soon the head kenneth away ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> where in the world have greater follies hap opened than with the pitiful ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And what in the world hath done more harm than the follies of the pitiful ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Woe unto all loving ones who do not possess an elevation which is above their pity ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus the devil once said unto me : Even God hath his own hell : that is his love unto men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And recently I heard the word said : God is dead he hath died of his pity for men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Beware of pity : a heavy cloud will one day come from it for men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , I understand about ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But remember this word also : All great love is lifted above all its pity , for it seemeth to create what it lovett ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Myself I sacrifice unto my love , and my neighbour as myself , thus kenneth the speech of all creators . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus spake Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF PRIESTS One day Zarathustra made a sign unto his disciples and spake unto them these words : Here are priests . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And though they are mine enemies , pass them quietly and with sleeping sword ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Among them also there are heroes many of them have suffered too much . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Hence they try to make others suffer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Evil friends they are : nothing is more vengeful than their submissiveness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And easily he defile himself who touched them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But my blood is kindred with theirs I would have my blood honoured even in theirs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when they had passed , Zarathustra was attacked by pain . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when he had fought with his pain a little while , he thus began to speak : I am sorry for these priests . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are contrary unto my taste , but that is a small matter unto me since I am dwelling among men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I suffer and have suffered with them : prisoners they are for me , and branded ones . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He whom they call Saviour put them into fetters : Into the fetters of false values and illusory words ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Oh , that some one would save them from their Saviour ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Once when the sea tossed them to and fro they believed they had landed on an island but , behold , it was a slumbering monster ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> False values and illusory words : these are the worst monsters for mortals : in them doom and waited long . <end>

<unchecked> <start> One night Zarathustra went through the forest with his disciples , and when seeking for a well , behold ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> Oh , how laughed my soul at his ugliness ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> With his breast raised and like those who draw in their breath thus he stood there , the august one , and silent Covered with ugly truths , the prey of his hunting , and rich with torn clothes many thorns also hung on him , but I saw no rose . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not yet had he learnt laughter and beauty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Frowning this hunter came back from the forest of perception . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He returned from the struggle with wild beasts but out of his seriousness a wild beast looked one not overcome ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Like a tiger still standish he there , about to jump but I care not for these strained souls my taste hath no favour for all these reserved ones . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And ye tell me , friends , that one cannon quarrel about taste and tasting ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But all life is a struggle about taste and tasting ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Taste that is at the same time weight and balance and the weighing one . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> for all living things that would try to live without struggle about weight and balance and weighing ones ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> And not until then shall I taste him and find him tasty . <end>

<unchecked> <start> straight into his sun . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Although he rested just now , his rest hath not yet lain down in the sun . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Unattainable by struggle is the beautiful for all eager will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A little more , a little less just that is here much , that is here the most . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To stand with your muscles relaxed and with your will harnessed , that is the hardest for all of you , ye august ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> When power become gracious and stepped down into beauty I call such stepping down . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And of no one I demand beauty with the same eagerness as just from thee , thou powerful one . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let thy goodness be thy last self overcoming ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Everything evil I expect from thee therefore I demand from thee what is good . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , I laughed many a time over the weaklings who thought themselves good because they had lame paws ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> For this is the secret of the soul . <end>

<unchecked> <start> When they give themselves the air of wisdom , I grow cold with their petty sayings and truths . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Thus they weave the stockings of the spirit ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> their heads and even if I should walk on mine own faults , I should still be above them and their heads . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Thus speaker justice . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And what I will they would not be allowed to will ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Since I came to know the body better , said Zarathustra unto one of his disciples , spirit hath been for me , as it were , spirit only , and all that is imperishable only a simile . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I heard thee say already , answered the disciple . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when thou sadist thus thou didst add : But the poets lie too much . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Why ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> said Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou asked why ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I am not of those who may be asked for their whys . <end>
<unchecked> <start> forsyth , is mine experience of yesterday ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is long since I found by experience the reasons for mine opinions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would I not require to be a barrel of memory , if I were to have my reasons with me ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even to keep mine opinions is too much for me and many a bird lieth off . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And sometimes indeed I find a bird in my dovecot , that hath come there but is strange unto me and trembled when I lay my hand on it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But what did Zarathustra once say unto thee ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> That the poets lie too much ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But Zarathustra is a poet also . <end>
<unchecked> <start> believes thou now that he spake the truth in this point ? <end>

<unchecked> <start> But Zarathustra shook his head and smiled . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Belief doth not make me blessed , said he , more especially not the belief in myself . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Besides we know too little and are bad learners . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus we are compelled to lie . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And which of us poets hath not unadulterated his wine ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Many a poisonous mishmash hath been brought about in our cellars many indescribable things have been done there . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And because we know little we like from our heart s heart the poor in spirit , especially if they are little young women ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And we are even desirous of the things which the little old women tell each other at night . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This we call in ourselves eternally feminine . <end>

<unchecked> <start> lying in the grass or by lonely slopes and cricket up his ears , learned something about the things which are between heaven and earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when feeling amorous emotions , the poets ever think that nature herself is in love with them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And that she stealth unto their ear , to whisper into it secret things and love batteries , of that they boast , and in it they take their pride in the presence of all mortals ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , there are so many things between heaven and earth of which poets only have dreamt ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And chiefly above heaven . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For all Gods are a simile of poets , an imposition by poets ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , we are always drawn upwards namely into the kingdom of clouds . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On these we place our coloured dolls and call them Gods and bondmen . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For they are just light enough for such chairs all these Gods and beyond men ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , how weary I am of all the inadequate things which are obstinately maintained to be actuality ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , how weary I am of poets ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Zarathustra so saying , his disciple was angry with him but was silent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And Zarathustra was silent also and his eye had turned inwards , as though he gazed into far distances . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At last he sighed and took breath . <end>
<unchecked> <start> but something is within me , that is of to morrow and the day after to morrow and the far future . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I became weary of poets , of the old and of the new . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Superficial all of them are , and shallow seas . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They did not think deep enough . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Therefore their feeling did not sink so deep as to reach the bottom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Some voluptuousness and some seriousness these have even been their best meditation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> As a breathing and vanishing of ghosts I regard all the strumming of their harp . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What have they known hitherto of the ardour of tones ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Besides they are not cleanly enough for me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All of them make their water muddy that it may seem deep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And they like to let themselves appear as reconciles . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But mediators and mixers they remain for me , and half and half ones and unclean ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas , it is true I have cast my net in their seas and tried to catch good fish but I always drew up the head of some old God . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus the sea gave a stone unto the hungry one . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And perhaps they themselves are born from the sea . <end>
<unchecked> <start> True , one finder pearls in them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> So much the more are they like unto the hard shell fish . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And instead of a soul I often found salt slime in them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> From the sea they learned even its vanity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is not the sea the peacock of peacocks ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even before the ugliest of all buffaloes it unfolded its tail and it never wearied of its lace fan of silver and silk . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Defiantly looked at it the buffalo , with soul nigh the sand , still higher the thicket , but highest the swamp . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is for it beauty and sea and peacock decoration ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> This simile I give unto poets . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , their mind itself is the peacock of peacocks , and a sea of vanity ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The mind of poets wished spectators , even if it were buffaloes ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I wearied of that mind and I see a time when it will weary of itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Changed already have I seen the poets , and their glance turned against themselves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Penitents of spirit I saw come . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They grew out of poets . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is an island in the sea not far from the blissful islands of Zarathustra in which a volcano smoke constantly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The folk , and especially the little old women among the folk , say that that island is set before the gate of the underworld . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But through the volcano there is a narrow path down , which leader unto that gate of the underworld . <end>
<unchecked> <start> About that time when Zarathustra lived on the blissful islands it came to pass that a ship cast anchor at that island on which the smoking mountain standish and the sailors of that ship went ashore in order to shoot rabbits ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But about the hour of noon , when the captain and his men had mustered again , they suddenly saw a man come through the air unto them , and a voice said distinctly : It is time ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is high time ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But when that person was highest unto them he passed by them flying quickly like a shadow , in the direction in which the volcano was situated they recognised with the greatest confusion that it was Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For all of them , except the captain , had seen him before , and they loved him , as the folk love , blending love and awe in equal parts . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lo there ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> said the old steersman , Zarathustra goethe unto hell ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> About the same time when these sailors landed at the fire island , a rumour went about that Zarathustra had disappeared . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And when his friends were asked they told how at night he had gone aboard a ship without saying whither he was going to voyage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus some anxiety arose . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But after three days the story of the sailors was added unto that anxiety and now everyone said that the devil had taken Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Although his disciples laughed at that gossip and one of them even said : I rather believe that Zarathustra hath taken the devil , at the bottom of their soul they were all full of sorrow and longing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus their joy was great when , on the fifth day , Zarathustra appeared among them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And this is the story of Zarathustra s conversation with the fiery dog : Earth , said he , hath a skin and that skin hath diseases . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One of these diseases , for example , is called : man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And another of these diseases is called fiery dog of it men have told and been told many lies . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To find out this secret I went beyond the sea . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And I have seen truth naked , verily ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> barefoot up to its neck . <end>
<unchecked> <start> THUS SPAKE ZARATHUSTRA , II Now I know the truth about that fiery dog and at the same time about all the devils of casting out and of revolution , of which not only little old women are afraid . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Come up , fiery dog , out of thy depth ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I shouted , and confess how deep that depth is ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whence cometh what thou shortest up ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou drinks enough at the sea that is betrayed by thy salt eloquence ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Verily , considering that thou art a dog of the depth thou takes thy food too much from the surface ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> At the highest I regard thee as a ventriloquist of earth , and whenever I heard devils of revolution and casting out speak , I found them to be like thee : salt , deceitful and shallow . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye understand how to roar and to darken with ashes ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye are the best swaggered and have sufficiently learnt the art of heating mud . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wherever ye are , there must mud be nigh , and many mud like , hollow , squeezed in things . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They seek to get into freedom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Freedom all of you like best to shout . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I have lost my belief in great events , whenever much shouting and smoke are round them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And believe me , friend Hellish Noise ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The greatest events are not our loudest but our smallest hours . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The world doth not revolve round the inventors of new noise , but round the inventors of new values inaudibly it turned . <end>
<unchecked> <start> OF GREAT EVENTS ii And now confess ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Little had actually happened when thy noise and smoke disappeared . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What matter that a town became a mummy , and a statue lay in the mud ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And this word I tell the subverted of statues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Probably the greatest folly is to throw salt into the sea , and statues into the mud . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the mud of your contempt the statue lay . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But that very fact is its law , that out of contempt life and living beauty grow again ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> With more godlike features it now arise , seducing by suffering and verily ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> it will thank you one day for subverting it , ye subverted ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But with this counsel I counsel kings and churches and ah that is weak from old age and virtue : allow yourselves to be subverted ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> In order that ye may recover life , and that virtue may recover you ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus I spake before the fiery dog then it interrupted me sullenly and asked : Church ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is that ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Church ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> I answered , that is a kind of state , viz . <end>
<unchecked> <start> the most deceitful kind . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But be quiet , thou hypocritical dog ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thou knows thy kin best , I suppose ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The state is a hypocritical dog like thyself like thyself it lieth to speak with smoke and roaring , in order to make believe , like thee , that it speaker out of the womb of things . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For it wished absolutely to be the most important animal on earth , the state . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And it is believed to be so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When I had said thus , the fiery dog behaved as if it were mad with envy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> it cried , the most important animal on earth ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And it is believed to be so ? <end>

<unchecked> <start> At last it became quieter , and its panting ceased . <end>

<unchecked> <start> And in order that I may also be right in future , let me speak unto thee of another fiery dog , that actually speaker out of the heart of earth . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Thus its heart willett . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What are for it ashes and smoke and hot phlegm ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> But gold and laughter it taketh out of the heart of earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For thou mayfest now know the heart of earth is of gold . <end>

<unchecked> <start> In shame it drew in its tail sorely cast down it said : Bow wow ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> and crept down into its cave . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus told Zarathustra . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But his disciples scarcely listened unto him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> So great was their desire to tell him about the sailors , the rabbits , and the flying man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What am I to think of that ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> said Zarathustra . <end>

<unchecked> <start> But it may have been my shadow . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I suppose ye have heard some things about the wanderer and his shadow ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But one thing is sure : I must keep it shorter , otherwise it spoiled my reputation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And Zarathustra shook his head once more and wondered . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What am I to think of that ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> he repeated . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For what is it high time ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And I saw a great sadness coming over men . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The best became weary of their works . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A doctrine went out , a belief ran with it : All is empty , all is equal , all hath been ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And from all hills it echoed : All is empty , all is equal , all hath been ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> True , we have reaped . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But why grew all our fruits rotten and brown ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> What hath fallen down from the evil moon last night ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> In vain hath been all work , our wine hath become poison , an evil eye hath burnt our fields and hearts yellow . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Dry all of us have become and when fire fallen down on us we become dust like ashes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Fire itself we have wearied out . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For us , all wells pined away even the sea receded from us . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All the soil is going to break , but the depth is not going to devour anything ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Alas ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> where is a sea left to be drowned in ? <end>

<unchecked> <start> Verily , we are already too weary to die . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now we wake on and live on in burial vaults ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus heard Zarathustra a fortune teller say and the prophecy touched his heart and changed him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He went about dreary and weary and he became like those of whom the fortune teller had spoken . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Alas , how can I save my light beyond it ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Would that it were not extinguished in that sadness ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> For it is meant to be a light for still remoter worlds , and for the remotest nights ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus afflicted Zarathustra went about . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And for three days he did not take any drink or food he had no rest and lost his speech . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At last it came to pass that he fell into a deep sleep . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But his disciples sat around him in long night watches and waited sorrowing , to see whether he would awake and speak again and recover from his affliction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This is the speech which Zarathustra made when he awoke . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But his voice sounded unto his disciples as though it came from a far distance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now listen unto the dream I dreamt , ye friends , and help me to find out its sense ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> A riddle it is still for me , that dream . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Its sense is hidden within it and caught in it , and lieth not yet over it with free wings . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I dreamt I had renounced all life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I had become a night watchman and grave watchman , there on the lonely castle of death in the mountains . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On high there I guarded death s coffins . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The damp vaults stood full of such signs of triumph . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Out of glass coffins , overcome life gazed at me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The odour of dusty I breathed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Sultry and dusty lay my soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And who could have aired his soul there ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Light of midnight was always round me , loneliness cowered beside me , and , as the third , the death stillness and rattle , the most wicked of all my female friends . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I had keys with me , the busiest of keys and I knew how to open with them the loudest creaking doors . <end>

<unchecked> <start> But still more terrible , strangling one s heart , it was when it became silent again and still round about , and I sat alone with that insidious silence . <end>

<unchecked> <start> What know I thereof ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But at last that came to pass which awakened me . <end>

<unchecked> <start> alpha ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> alpha ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> alpha ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Who carried his ashes unto the mountains ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> And I pressed the key and tried to lift the door , and exerted myself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But it was not yet opened a finger s breadth Then an impetuous wind tore its two halves apart . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whistling , whizzing , and buzzing it threw a black coffin at me . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And amidst the roaring and whistling and whizzing the coffin brake and spat out a thousandfold laughter . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And out of a thousand caricatures of children , angels , owls , fools , and butterflies as big as children , something laughed and mocked and roared at me . <end>
